Topic: Logic
Context: The basis of life-the main component of protein is an amino acid molecule.It is an organic molecule.Although people have not directly observed amino acid molecules in cosmic space, scientists have used hydrogen, water, oxygen, methane and formaldehyde in the laboratory to simulate the natural conditions of space.Kinds of amino acids.The raw materials used to synthesize amino acids are abundant in interstellar molecules.It is not difficult to imagine that there must also be amino acid molecules in the universe.As long as there is an appropriate environment, they may be transformed into proteins and further develop into organic life.According to this speculation, there are living bodies on other planets than the earth, and may even be living bodies with higher intelligence.
Question: Which of the following is true to best refute the above speculation?
Choices:
  A: There is a huge difference between the process of developing from protein to organic life and the process from organic molecules to protein
  B: Higher intelligence is not only a product of material evolution, but also a product of continuous socialization
  C: In the natural environment, the synthesis of amino acid molecules from existing interstellar molecules is a small probability event
  D: Some interstellar molecules are not found in the Earth ’s environment, and they are still not available in the laboratory
Response 0:
Thought:
  The given context states that it is possible for there to be life on other planets, as long as the environment is appropriate for the synthesis of amino acid molecules.
  The question asks for the choice that refutes this speculation.
  Choice A does not necessarily refute the speculation, as it only mentions a difference in the process.
  Choice B also does not refute the speculation, as it only suggests that intelligence is not solely dependent on biological evolution.
  Choice D is not relevant to the speculation.
  Choice C is the most relevant, as it suggests that the synthesis of amino acid molecules is a low probability event in natural environments. This would make it less likely for there to be life on other planets.
  Therefore, the answer is C: In the natural environment, the synthesis of amino acid molecules from existing interstellar molecules is a small probability event.
Action: Answer("C")

Topic: Logic
Context: Placebo effect" refers to the phenomenon of letting patients take fake drugs that have no effect at all without knowing it, but they can get the same or better effects than real drugs.The "placebo effect" has been supported by many clinical studies.One explanation for this phenomenon is that human expectations for the future will change the physiological state of the brain, which in turn will cause physiological changes throughout the body.
Question: The following statements can support the above explanation, except
Choices:
  A: The placebo effect is the result of a combination of factors.
  B: Placebo has no effect on Alzheimer's patients who have lost their expected future abilities.
  C: Some patients do not believe that the treatment will be effective.Although they have been treated normally, their condition has worsened.
  D: Inject the subject with normal saline and make him believe that it is an analgesic.The subject's brain then secretes the analgesic endorphin.
Response 0:
Thought:
  The explanation for the "placebo effect" is that human expectations for the future can change the physiological state of the brain, which causes physiological changes throughout the body.
  Statement A supports the explanation.
  Statement B contradicts the explanation.
  Statement C supports the explanation.
  Statement D supports the explanation.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Placebo has no effect on Alzheimer's patients who have lost their expected future abilities.

  Statement B contradicts the explanation because it suggests that the placebo effect isn't effective for patients who do not have future expectations, and so it does not support the explanation.

Topic: Logic
Context: There is an authoritative public opinion polling agency that investigates the causes of the terrorist attacks on September 11, and found that 40% of the people believed that they were caused by unfair foreign policy of the United States, and 55% It is believed that it is due to the conflict between Islamic civilization and Western civilization.23% of people believe that it is due to the evil nature of terrorists, and 19% of them did not express their views.
Question: Which of the following best explains the contradictory statement above?
Choices:
  A: The sampling of the survey sample is not random and therefore not representative.
  B: Some respondents later changed their views.
  C: Many investigators believe that the causes of the "September 11" terrorist attacks were not single but compound.
  D: There are technical errors in the calculation of the investigation results.
Response 0:

The statement does not imply any technical errors in calculation, and respondents did not change their views. 
  Therefore, the most likely reason for the contradiction is that many investigators believe that the causes of "September 11" terrorist attacks were not single, but compound. Hence, the answer is C: Many investigators believe that the causes of the "September 11" terrorist attacks were not single but compound.

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 4 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: There are 6 scholars F, G, J, L, M, and N, who will speak at a logical meeting, and the speeches are arranged in the following order? (1) Each speaker speaks only once, and only once at the same time By.(2) Three speakers speak before lunch, and the other three speak after lunch.(3) G must speak before lunch.(4) Only one speaker is between M and N.(5) F speaks in the first or third place.
Question: If the speeches of M and N are separated by lunch, which of the following lists all speakers that can be arranged between M and N?
Choices:
  A: G, J
  C: F, G, J
  B: J, L
  D: F, G, J, L
Response 0:
Thought: 
  M and N are separated by lunch means M and N must speak in positions 2 and 5 in some order (either M is in 2 and N in 5, or N is in 2 and M in 5).
  G must speak before lunch, which means G must speak in either position 1, 2, or 3.
  Then, F is in either position 1 or 3 but not in position 2.
  From (4), there is only 1 speaker between M and N.
  Therefore, the speaker in position 4 must be one of the choices to arrange between M and N.
  There is only one option that satisfies all the given conditions, which is J.
  So, J should be the speaker to arrange between M and N.
  Now, we have three positions left (1, 3 and 6) and two speakers (F and either L or J)
  Either F, G, and L or G, F, and L can be arranged in positions 1, 3, and 6.
  F, G, and J or G, F, and J can be arranged in positions 1, 2, and 3.
  Therefore, the speakers that can be arranged between M and N are J.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  The order of the speeches is divided into two parts, before lunch and after lunch, with three speeches each. G speaks before lunch, which means M and N speak after lunch.
  F speaks in the first or third place. If F speaks in the first place, N will speak in the last one, and if F speaks in the third place, M would speak first after lunch.
  There's only one person between M and N, so N only speaks before L or J, and M speaks after J or G.
  Therefore, J will always be in between M and N, and G will be before J, while only L or F can be after N.
  Therefore, the list of speakers that can be arranged between M and N is only C: F, G, J.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  The order of speeches: F_J_L_M_N_G or G_F_J_N_M_L (Since G must speak before lunch, F speaks in the first or third place and only one speaker is between M and N).
  If M and N are separated by lunch, then 3 speakers speak before lunch. Therefore, M and N cannot be the first three speakers. 
  
  If M and N are the last two speakers, then only one speaker is left to speak before lunch. Since G must speak before lunch, G must be the one who speaks before lunch. There remains only one speaker to speak after lunch, which will be F. Therefore, the order of speeches will be: G, J, L, F, M, N.
  The only possible arrangement of the speakers between M and N is J and L.
  
  (A), (C), and (D) all contain G which can only speak before lunch. So the answer must include only J and L.
  
Action: Answer("B")

  The only possible arrangement of speakers between M and N is GJ or JG, where G speaks in the first place, and J speaks in the second place.
  Therefore the answer is A: G, J.

  Therefore, it is impossible for Y to accompany singers G and H.

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 12 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: One of the strictest laws in history to ban smoking, although it has not yet banned people from smoking in their homes, it prohibits people from smoking in all public places and workplaces.If this law is strictly enforced, it will completely protect workers from second-hand smoke.
Question: If which of the following statements is true, the above argument is weakened most effectively?
Choices:
  A: The exhaust of cars from people commuting to work is much more harmful than smoking second-hand smoke.
  B: Persons such as tutors, nurses, hourly workers, etc.all work at the employer ’s home.
  C: No piece of legislation and its implementation can fully realize the intent of the legislator.
  D: This smoking control law overestimates the dangers of smoking secondhand smoke.
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The argument claims that the law will completely protect workers from second-hand smoke in all public places and workplaces.
  To weaken the argument, we need to find a true statement that contradicts the conclusion that the law will completely protect workers.
  Option A discussing car exhaust is irrelevant to the argument about the effectiveness of the strict smoking ban law.
  Option B discussing where some people work is also irrelevant to the argument about the effectiveness of the strict smoking ban law.
  Option C, which claims that no law can fully realize its intent, may be a valid criticism of the effectiveness of the law. 
  However, it is a broad statement that is not specific to smoking or this particular law. 
  Option D, which states that the law overestimates the dangers of smoking secondhand smoke, if true, would weaken the argument that the law would completely protect workers from second-hand smoke.
  Therefore, the answer is D: This smoking control law overestimates the dangers of smoking secondhand smoke.

  A: Those women who often eat celery pay more attention to fitness, and fitness consumes a lot of physical energy, is very tired, and suppresses the aggressive mood.

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 22 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: In a cooking competition, the chef is required to make one hot dish and one cold dish, and the results are evaluated as "top grade", "middle grade", and "bottom grade".If each result of the chef is not lower than that of Chef B, and at least one item is higher than Chef B, it is said that "Chef A is more skilled than Chef B".There are a number of existing chefs, none of them is more skilled than the other, and no two people have the same hot dishes and cold dishes.
Question: How many chefs can meet the above conditions?
Choices:
  A: unconfirmed
  B: 9 people
  C: 6 people
  D: 3 people
Response 0:
Thought:
  There are no two chefs having the same hot dishes and cold dishes. 
  Assume we have three categories of results: top, middle, bottom. Since there are no two chefs having the same hot dishes and cold dishes, the maximum number of top grade results is the same as the maximum number of bottom grade results. Half of the chefs will be in the top grade, half of the chefs will be at the bottom grade, and the other half will be in the middle grade. Therefore, in order for Chef A to be more skilled than Chef B, Chef A must obtain first place in both the hot and cold dishes and Chef B must obtain second place.
  Select any two chefs, one of them must be ranked higher than the other. Therefore, if the two chefs are out of consideration for each other, the eight chefs who are not paired with them can be paired with each other. Therefore, there are 8/2 = 4 pairs of chefs. So the answer = 4*2=8 chefs.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Each chef has different hot dishes and cold dishes - this means that there's no repetition of the dishes for each chef.
  To be considered more skilled than Chef B, Chef A must have at least one dish ranked higher than Chef B's dishes and not have any dishes that are ranked lower than Chef B's dishes.
  There are a total of six dishes per chef.
  If no two people have the same hot and cold dishes, that means there are 6 factorial (6!) permutations of dishes for a single chef.
  If we have a total of N chefs, then there are N * 6! permutations of dishes that need to be evaluated.
  Given this constraint, we can start from N = 3 and work our way upwards.

Trial:
  We can try listing out the permutations for 3 chefs and see if it agrees with our rules:
    Chef 1: A1  B1  C1  D1  E1  F1
    Chef 2: A2  B2  C2  D2  E2  F2
    Chef 3: A3  B3  C3  D3  E3  F3
    
    There are 3 factorial (3!) ways that chef orders can be arranged, so we can get 6 different permutations of chefs.
    For each permutation, we can compare the skills of the chefs.
    If we end up with Chef A being more skilled than Chef B for all possible combinations, then we know that N = 3 is a valid answer.
  However, listing out all the combinations would be tiresome, so for now, let's try another approach.

Logic:
  For 3 chefs, there are a total of 6! * 3 permutations of dishes to be evaluated.
  Since Chef A cannot be less skilled than Chef B in every permutation:
    - Chef A has to have at least 1 dish that ranks higher than Chef B's
    - There are 5 other dishes that Chef A can use to be compared with Chef B's
    - Since Chef B is not the most skilled, there has to be another chef that has better dishes than Chef B.
    - This chef, Chef C, can either have a dish that beats Chef B's or loses to Chef B's, or they are evenly matched.
    - If they are evenly matched, then we can eliminate Chef B as the lower skilled chef.
    - If Chef C has a better dish than Chef B, then Chef A has to beat Chef C in that category.
    - If Chef C has a worse dish than Chef B, then Chef A has to beat Chef C in at least two categories.
    - This means that Chef A has to have at least 3 dishes that are ranked higher than Chef B's (1 against Chef B, and 2 against Chef C).

Answer: Answer("D")  - 3 people

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 23 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: Zhang Qiang? When the economy in a region is sluggish, many people are unemployed, so they reduce their living expenses, resulting in more unemployment and worsening the economy.The economy continued to deteriorate, and finally prices fell to the lowest point.Low prices have stimulated people to increase their living consumption, and increased consumption has led to improved economic conditions.Li Ming? If people are unemployed, they will not be able to increase their consumption, nor will they have the money to buy goods other than the necessities of life.Therefore, falling prices to the lowest point will not lead to an improvement in economic conditions.
Question: If the following statement is true, which one can best weaken Li Ming's rebuttal to Zhang Qiang?
Choices:
  A: After the economic situation improves, the company will hire more people, and many people who are reemployed will buy the goods that have been delayed.
  B: Even if the economic situation continues to deteriorate, consumers still believe that the economic situation will eventually improve.
  C: Even when the economy is extremely deteriorating, the unemployed must continue to buy necessities such as food.
  D: During the period of economic deterioration, even unemployed people will compress expenditures; when prices fall to the lowest point, they will have savings for consumption.
Response 0:
Thought: 
Li Ming argues that if people are unemployed, they will not have the money to buy goods other than the necessities of life, so falling prices to the lowest point will not lead to an improvement in economic conditions.
We need to find a statement which can counter Li Ming's argument by providing evidence that even unemployed people can still increase their consumption behavior under specific situations.
Option A provides evidence that people who were reemployed would buy the goods that have been delayed.
Option B provides no evidence that unemployed people can increase their consumption behavior.
Option C does not weaken Li Ming's rebuttal since even when the economy is extremely deteriorating, the unemployed must continue to buy necessities such as food.
Option D provides evidence that people can still compress expenditures during the period of economic deterioration and have savings for consumption. This statement can weaken Li Ming's point and provide evidence of a specific situation where even unemployed people can increase their consumption behavior under specific situations.
Therefore, the answer is D: During the period of economic deterioration, even unemployed people will compress expenditures; when prices fall to the lowest point, they will have savings for consumption. 
Action: Answer("D")

  Choice C is trying to argue that the unemployed must continue to buy necessities, but this statement does not address the points made by Zhang Qiang and Li Ming.
  Choice D is about the savings that unemployed people may have, it argues that some of them can have savings and, thus, can increase their consumption.
  Therefore, choice D best weakens Li Ming's rebuttal to Zhang Qiang.

Context: A theater plans to perform 7 repertoires in the 7 weeks of the fall, they are F, G., J, K, O, R, S.One repertoire is performed every week, and each repertoire is exactly one week.The repertoire must meet the following conditions? (1) G must be performed in the third week.(2) O and S cannot perform continuously.(3) K must be arranged before J and S.(4) F and J must be arranged to perform in two consecutive weeks.
Question: If S is scheduled for the sixth week, then which week must R be scheduled?
Choices:
  A: the second week
  B: Fourth week
  C: fifth week
  D: Seventh week
Response 0:
Thought:
  There are 7 weeks to perform 7 repertoires, so one is performed each week. 
  If S is scheduled for the sixth week, then G must be scheduled in the third week. 
  According to (2), O cannot be scheduled in the seventh week, so it must be scheduled for either the 1st or 2nd week. 
  F and J must be arranged to perform in two consecutive weeks, therefore, they must be scheduled in either the fourth and fifth weeks or the fifth and sixth weeks. 
  K must be arranged before J and S, so K must be performed earlier than S. Therefore, the only possible places for K are the first, second, or fourth week. 
  If K is scheduled for the second week, G is scheduled for the third week, and S is slotted for the sixth week, then we are left with the following arrangement: 
  Week 1: O or R
  Week 2: K 
  Week 3: G 
  Week 4: J or R
  Week 5: F
  Week 6: S 
  Week 7: O or R. 
  Therefore, R must be scheduled for either the first or seventh week.
  Neither O or R must be scheduled for the same consecutive weeks according to (2), thus, R must be scheduled in the first week. 
  The answer is A: the second week.

Context: The traditional view believes that the origin of the names of the Eight Diagrams and Sixty-four Diagrams in Zhouyi is fiction, or there is no meaning.There is no other explanation.The fiction says that the Eight Diagrams are named after the name of an object, For example, Qiangua is the heaven, and Qian is the ancient Chinese character, so it is named Qian; in the sense of meaning, the image of hexagrams represents the principle of things, and its rationality is taken as the name of a hexagram.The Lord is supple, so the hexagram is Kun, and Kun is the meaning of suppleness
Question: Which of the following statements is true, which most seriously shakes the traditional view of the origin of the Gua name?
Choices:
  A: The reason why the two hexagrams of Qiankun ranks first among the sixty-four hexagrams is because the Qian gua represents heaven and the Kun gua represents earth.
  B: The hexagram name cannot be explained by the orientation theory alone, nor can it be explained by the sense of meaning alone.Only by combining the two can we give an explanation of all hexagram names
  C: Although there are many different explanations for the origin of the Gua name, it is inseparable from its sect, either attributed to the theory of fetching images, or attributed to the theory of fetching meanings
  D: The name of the hexagram comes from the account of the narration of the hexagram.Kun Guazhan asked about the loss of the horse.At the beginning, he had three elephants.He believed that the horse could be found and was named Kun.

  A states that the reason why the two hexagrams of Qiankun ranks first among the sixty-four hexagrams is because the Qian gua represents heaven and the Kun gua represents earth. This statement does not necessarily shake the traditional view, and it actually supports it.

Topic: Logic
Context: There are 6 warehouses in a warehouse, in order from 1 to 6.There are 6 kinds of goods F, G, L, M, P, T.Each warehouse stores exactly one of 6 kinds of goods, and different kinds of goods cannot be stored in the same warehouse.The following conditions must also be met when storing goods? (1) The warehouse number for storing G is larger than that for storing L (2) The warehouse number storing L is larger than the warehouse number storing T.(3) The warehouse number storing P is larger than the warehouse number storing F.(4) The warehouse storing T is next to the warehouse storing P.
Question: Which of the following must be false?
Choices:
  A: The warehouse storing F is next to the warehouse storing M
  B: The warehouse storing G is next to the warehouse storing M
  C: The warehouse storing P is next to the warehouse storing L
  D: The warehouse storing L is next to the warehouse storing F
Response 0:
Thought:
  Put the conditions together: 
  F < P, L < T < P, G > L, T next to P
  Therefore, the sequence of the warehouse is: F, P, _, T, L, G or P, F, T, _, G, L
  The possibilities that must be false are:
  A: F is next to M, but there is no space next to F in the sequence.
  B: G is next to M. Because G > L, L can only be in position 4th or 5th. In these two cases, however, there is no warehouse to place G next to L.
  C: P is next to L. Because F < P, F can only be placed in the first position. In this case, there is no space to put L in.
  D: L is next to F. This situation can only be embodied in the first sequence. T must be in the fourth position, and there is no space to place L next to F.
  Therefore, the answer is A: The warehouse storing F is next to the warehouse storing M. 
Action: Answer("A")

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 29 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: A street comprehensive governance committee has 6 members? F, G, H, I, M and P.Each of these members must be a member of at least one of the three sub-committees under the Comprehensive Governance Committee.Each sub-committee is composed of 3 different members.The known information is as follows? one of the six members serves as a member of three subcommittees.F is not a member of the same subcommittee as G.H is not a member of the same subcommittee as I.
Question: Which of the following statements must be true?
Choices:
  A: M and P are members of a subcommittee.
  B: F and H are members of a subcommittee.
  C: G and I are members of a subcommittee.
  D: 1 member of any sub-committee.
Response 0:
Thought: 
  There are three sub-committees, each composed of three different members.
  One member serves as a member of three sub-committees.
  The remaining five members should serve as members of at least one sub-committee each.
  From the given information, F and G, and H and I, respectively, cannot be members of the same subcommittee.
  Therefore, the members in a subcommittee are (1) F; (2) G and either H or I; (3) any member except F, G, H, or I along with the member not in the same subcommittee as G or I.
  Therefore, statement A cannot be guaranteed, statement B is impossible since F and H cannot be members of the same subcommittee, statement C is impossible since G and I cannot be members of the same subcommittee, and statement D is too broad to be guaranteed.
  Thus, the answer must be None of the Above.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Three sub-committees each has 3 different members, so there must be a total of 9 members in the sub-committees.
  One of the six members serves as a member of three subcommittees, so there are 5 members to fill 8 spots.
  Since F is not a member of the same subcommittee as G, F cannot be in the same sub-committees as G. Similarly, H cannot be in the same sub-committees as I.
  Thus, F, G, and H must be each in different sub-committees.
  So, consider the following:
  - F must be in the same sub-committees as M and P in order to serve in three subcommittees.
  - G and H cannot be in the same sub-committee as I, so G and I must be in different sub-committees and same for H and I.
  - Therefore, M and P must be the only two members left that can be in a subcommittee together.
  - The remaining spots must be filled by G, H, and I.
  - Thus, it must be true that M and P are members of a sub-committee. (Choice A)
  - It is not necessarily true that F and H are members of a sub-committee. (Choice B)
  - It is not necessarily true that G and I are members of a sub-committee. (Choice C)
  - There must be at least one member of any sub-committee, but this statement is too general to be a must-be-true statement. (Choice D)
  
Action: Answer("A")

  C: Sixth on L

Choices:
  A: Only those who do what they want can do it to others.
  B: If you want, then give it to others.
  C: Don't treat others unless you want to.
  D: Whatever is applied to people should be what they want.
Response 0:
Thought:
  The sentence is a negative command, advising against causing others the harm that one would not want done unto themselves.
  A: is not a logical inference, since the statement doesn't mention anything about who is obligated to do things or reference any action at all. 
  B and C: are both variations of the original sentence and can be inferred from it.
  D: suggests an idea of equality between how one treats themselves and others, which can be inferred from the statement.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Only those who do what they want can do it to others.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The sentence states that you should not do to others what you do not want them to do to you; this is the Golden Rule or Law of Reciprocity.

  Option B seems to be a logical inference from the sentence, if you don't want someone else to do something that you're considering doing to them, then you shouldn't do it.
  Option C also seems to be a logical inference from the sentence, because it basically restates the sentence.
  Option D does not logically follow, because the sentence is talking about what you should do to others, and not about what should be applied to people.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Whatever is applied to people should be what they want.

Question: Which of the following may list the final distribution of these 7 employees?
Choices:
  A: Public Relations Department? W; Production Department? F, H, Y; Sales Department? G, I, X
  B: Public Relations Department? W; Production Department? G, I, X; Sales Department? F, H, Y
  C: Public Relations Department? X; Production Department? F, G, H; Sales Department? I, Y, W
  D: Public Relations Department? X; Production Department? F, I, W; Sales Department? G, H, Y
Response 0:

- H and Y must be allocated in the same department.

- If X is allocated in the sales department, W is allocated in the production department.
- F must be allocated in the production department.
- We need to allocate one person in the public relations department, three people in the production department, and three people in the sales department.

- According to condition (2), F and G cannot be allocated in the same department, so G is in the public relations department.

- So, Public Relations Department will have G, Production Department will have F, H, and W, and Sales Department will have X, Y, and I.
- The answer is D: Public Relations Department? X; Production Department? F, I, W; Sales Department? G, H, Y.

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 58 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: Researchers in a country reported that they found meteorites about 200 million years old in the strata of a certain area, and they were probably traces of flying objects when a huge meteorite hit the present province of Quebec, Canada.The clay layer with a thickness of about 5 cm also contains high concentrations of elements such as iridium and platinum, which are 50 to 2000 times the concentration normally found on the ground.In addition, this rock also contains special minerals in the formation of the late Bacques.Since the upper and lower strata also contain marine plankton fossils, it can be determined that the impact period was about 215 million years ago.
Question: Which of the following, if true, would best support the above research findings?
Choices:
  A: The rock was formed after the accumulation layer of the deep seabed in the ancient times exposed above the ground
  B: In the late Paleozoic Triassic (approximately 200 million to 237 million years ago) ammonite and other species were extinct on a large scale
  C: Elements such as iridium and platinum are peculiar to meteorites and usually only exist in trace amounts on the surface
  D: In ancient times, there have been many incidents of meteorite impacting the earth
Response 0:
Thought:
The researchers found that the meteorites were probably traces of a huge meteorite that hit Quebec province about 215 million years ago. They also found high concentrations of iridium and platinum, minerals from the formation of the late Bacques, and marine plankton fossils. Therefore, we need a statement that strengthens and supports these findings.
Option A is talking about the formation of the rock, which is not relevant to the stated facts.
Option B discusses extinction of some species but it has nothing to do with meteorites.
Option C supports the fact that the high concentration of elements like iridium and platinum in the rock supports the meteorite impact theory, so it is correct.
Option D mentions the meteorite impacts which may exist in the past, but nothing is mentioned about their connection to the present findings in the province of Quebec. So, option D is not relevant to the given facts.
Thus, the answer is C: Elements such as iridium and platinum are peculiar to meteorites and usually only exist in trace amounts on the surface.

Topic: Logic
Context: The members of the printing group and the binding group are mainly from the following seven employees-F, G, H, J, K, L and M.The members of each group must meet the following conditions? (1) Each group has at least 3 employees .(2) F and K cannot be in the same group.(3) If K is in a certain group, J must also be in this group.(4) M is at least one of the members of these two groups.(5) At least one of the same employees in both groups.
Question: If both K and L are members of both groups, and the printing group has exactly three members, which of the following statements must be true?
Choices:
  A: F in printing group
  B: F in the binding group
  C: G in the printing group
  D: M in the bookbinding group
Response 0:
Thought:
  K and L are members of both groups.
  The printing group has exactly three members.
  Therefore, one of K and L must be assigned to the binding group while the other is assigned to the printing group.
  If K is in the binding group, then J must also be a member of the binding group, so the printing group must have M and at least one of F, G, and H. (Condition 3 is true because K is in a certain group.)
  If K is in the printing group, then the printing group must have L and at least one of F, G, and H. (Conditions 1, 2, 4, and 5 are true.)
  The options are:
  A: F in printing group
      This statement could be true or false since we do not know whether K is in the binding group or the printing group.
  B: F in the binding group
      The statement could be true or false since we do not know whether K is in the binding group or the printing group.
  C: G in the printing group
      This statement could be true or false since we do not know whether K is in the binding group or the printing group.
  D: M in the bookbinding group
      This statement must be true because M is at least one of the members of the two groups, and K and L are in both groups. M is, therefore, a member of the binding group.
      
Therefore, the answer is D: M in the bookbinding group.
Response 1:
Thought:
  Both K and L are members of both groups. Therefore, K and L are not in the same group since each group has at least three employees.
  Since K is in both groups, J must also be in the group where K is a member. Therefore, the group with K and L must have J in it.
  Let's assume F is in the printing group, this means [G, H, J, K, L, M] are left to be distributed in two groups (printing and binding).
  Printing group has exactly three members, that means either F or L is not in the printing group.
  If F is not in the printing group, then {G, H, J, K, L, M} are to be divided into {F, K, and one person from {G, H, L, M}} and {remaining 3 persons}. This indicates that two employees will be present in both the groups, but we already know that this is a condition that already exists.
  Hence it is not possible that F is not in the printing group. That means F must be in the printing group.
  If F is in the printing group, then only one employee is left from {G, H, L, M} that can be present in the printing group. Since we already have J present in this group, that means M and either L or G will be in the Binding group.
  As M is at least one of the members of these two groups, this condition is satisfied.
  So we conclude that F is in the printing group, and G and M are in the binding group.
  Hence the statement "M in the bookbinding group" must be true.

(1) If G or H is arranged to play, they must be in the front.Bit.(2) If K is scheduled to play, he must be in the middle.(3) If L is scheduled to play, he must be on team 1.(4) Neither P nor K can be in the same team as N.(5) P cannot be in the same team as Q.(6) If H is in team 2, Q is in the middle of team 1.

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 76 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: There are 6 warehouses in a warehouse, in order from 1 to 6.There are 6 kinds of goods F, G, L, M, P, T.Each warehouse stores exactly one of 6 kinds of goods, and different kinds of goods cannot be stored in the same warehouse.The following conditions must also be met when storing goods? (1) The warehouse number for storing G is larger than the warehouse number for storing L.(2) The warehouse number storing L is larger than the warehouse number storing T.(3) The warehouse number storing P is larger than the warehouse number storing F.(4) The warehouse storing T is next to the warehouse storing P.
Question: If there is exactly one warehouse between the warehouse where M is stored and the warehouse where G is stored, how many kinds of goods are stored in the warehouse?
Choices:
  A: 2 rooms
  B: 3 rooms
  C: 4
  D: 5 rooms
Response 0:
Thought:
 - There is exactly one warehouse between the warehouse storing M and the warehouse storing G.
 - Warehouse number for storing G is greater than the warehouse number for storing L.
 - Warehouse number storing L > Warehouse number storing T.
 - Warehouse storing P is greater than warehouse storing F.
 - Warehouse storing T is next to the warehouse storing P.
 - We need to find how many kinds of goods are stored in the warehouse.
 
To find the answer, we can start by identifying the warehouses that we know the locations of:
- From condition (3), we know P is stored in a warehouse with a lower number than F, meaning P is stored in warehouse 1 or 2.
- From condition (4), we know that T is either stored in warehouse 3 or 5.
- From condition (2), we know that the warehouse storing L is warehouse 6.
- From condition (1), we know that G cannot be stored in warehouse 2 or 3. This means G is stored in either warehouse 4, 5, or 6.
- Because M must be one warehouse away from G, this means M is stored in warehouse 3 or 5.

Knowing the above information, we can determine the kinds of goods stored in each warehouse:
- Warehouse 1: P
- Warehouse 2: F
- Warehouse 3: M or T
- Warehouse 4: None
- Warehouse 5: G or T
- Warehouse 6: L

We can see that there are 4 kinds of goods stored in the warehouse: P, F, M or T, and L or G.
Therefore, the answer is C: 4.

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 77 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: I can relate some external symbols to some inner events, for example, to associate moaning and face distortion with the feeling of pain.I learned from the pain experience that when I feel pain, I often moan and twist my face.Therefore, once I see that others have the same external signs, I take it for granted that they also have the same inner activity events as me.After all, between me and others, the behavior and normal physiological functions are obviously similar.Why aren't they similar in inner activities?
Question: Which of the following can most strongly support the above argument?
Choices:

Topic: Logic
Context: The lower the credit rating of the borrower, the higher the cost of borrowing and the higher the rate of return for the creditor.On August 5, 2011, S & P downgraded the US sovereign credit rating from AAA to AA +.According to common sense, investors should reduce their holdings of U.S.Treasury bonds when they are in a safe haven, thereby pushing their prices down and yields rising.However, on August 8, the price of US Treasury bonds rose, and the yield fell, and the yield of the latest 10-year US Treasury bond fell to 2.34%, a new low this year.
Question: If any of the following statements are true, can we best explain the above-mentioned violation of common sense?
Choices:
  A: On the evening of August 5, the US Treasury responded that S & P had a $ 2 trillion error in its rating calculations.
  B: Compared with the bonds of the European Union, Japan and other countries, US Treasuries are still relatively safe and liquid investment products.
  C: After the US sovereign credit rating was lowered, Russia began to reduce its holdings of US Treasury bonds, while China still increased its holdings of US Treasury bonds.
  D: In order to break the monopoly of three US rating agencies including S & P, the EU plans to establish a European credit rating agency.
Response 0:
Thought:
  The question asks if any of the following statements can explain the violation of common sense.
  The argument suggests that the price of US Treasury bonds should go down and the yield rise after the credit rating is downgraded.
  However, on August 8, the price of US Treasury Bonds rose, and the yield fell.
  If any of the following statements can explain this violation of common sense, then choose that statement as the answer.
  Statement A, C, and D do not directly provide an explanation for the violation of common sense.
  Statement B, however, does provide a reason for the violation of common sense. When the bonds of other countries become less favorable, investors may still turn to US Treasuries despite the lower credit rating. Therefore, the demand for Treasuries may still increase and drive up prices and lower yields.
  The answer is B: Compared with the bonds of the European Union, Japan, and other countries, US Treasuries are still relatively safe and liquid investment products.

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Logic
Context: A music producer is recording 7 albums one after another? F, G, H, J, K, L and M, but it is not necessary to record in this order.When arranging the sequence of recording these 7 albums, the following conditions must be met? (l) F must be ranked second.(2) J cannot be ranked seventh.(3) G can neither be directly in front of H nor immediately after H.(4) H must be somewhere in front of L.(5) L must be somewhere before M.
Question: If M is somewhere before J and somewhere before K, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: K seventh
  B: L third
  C: H is either in front of F or immediately after F
  D: L either immediately before G or immediately after G
Response 0:
Thought: 
  M is before J and before K.
  We know F is second, therefore we can start the sequence like this: _F______
  According to condition (2), J is not seventh. Therefore, it is either fourth, fifth, or sixth.
  According to condition (5), L should be before M. Therefore, the arrangement should look like this: _F_L__M
  Now consider condition (4), which states that H must be somewhere in front of L. We have two possible arrangements: _F_HLM or H_FLM.
  Let's consider those two arrangements separately. 
  
  If H is in front of F (_FHLM), then G must be fifth and J must be sixth, so the remaining sequence is GFHLMJ. 
  Now, according to condition (3), G can neither be directly in front of H nor immediately after H, which means that G cannot be fourth or sixth. Therefore, K must be fourth, and the remaining sequence is GKFHLMJ. In this arrangement, we can see that L is not immediately before or after G, therefore L cannot be third and choice B is incorrect. Also, H is not immediately after or in front of F, it is after K, therefore choice C is incorrect. Therefore, the answer must be either A or D.
  
  If H is immediately after F (_FHML), then J must be sixth and G must be seventh, so the remaining sequence is FHLMJG. Now, according to condition (3), G cannot be immediately after or in front of H, which means that G cannot be seventh or fourth. Therefore, K must be seventh, and the remaining sequence is FHLMJGK. In this arrangement, L is immediately after G and is not immediately before G which means that choice D is incorrect. Therefore, the answer must be A.
  
  Therefore, the correct answer is A: K seventh.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We need to check which of the options must always be true based on the given conditions.
  M is somewhere before J and somewhere before K: M is before J and K.
  H must be somewhere in front of L and L must be somewhere before M: H-L-M.
  Therefore, the possible remaining order is F-G-H-L-M-K-J.
  K must be ranked seventh: not necessarily true.
  L cannot be ranked third as H must be placed before L: not true.
  H is either in front of F or immediately after F: true, as the only possible place for F is second and H can be third or fourth.
  L either immediately before G or immediately after G: true, as L and G must be in that order.
  
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  We know that M is before J and K.
  We also know that L must be before M. Therefore L must come before J and K too.
  Since F is ranked second, that means G and H must be either ranked first, third, fourth, fifth or sixth.
  From condition (2), we know that J cannot be ranked seventh, which means J must be one of the first six albums.
  Condition (4) tells us that H must be somewhere in front of L. So, both H and L must come after F.
  From condition (3), we know that G cannot be directly in front of H nor immediately after H. Therefore, G can only be ranked first or fifth.
  Combining these conditions, we can deduce that the only possible arrangement for these seven albums is F G _ H _ L M or F G _ H L M, where the blank spaces can be filled by J or K in any order.
  In both cases, we can see that H is either in front of F or immediately after F.
  Therefore, the answer is C: H is either in front of F or immediately after F.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 3:
Thought:
  The order of albums is F * * * * * *. There are 5 spaces left.
  J is not ranked seventh, so there are 4 spaces left for J.
  G can neither be directly in front of H nor immediately after H.
  - If G is in front of H (H * * * * * *), L must be between G and H, 
    so G and H have at most 3 choices of placement (positions 2 to 4).
    And L and M must be in positions 6 and 7 because L must be somewhere before M.
    There are only two potential spaces for J (positions 5 and 6), so J must be in position 5.
    Therefore, the order is F H L G M J.
  - If G is behind H (* * * H * * *), L and M can be placed anywhere between 3 and 7 where L is before M.
    There are no restrictions on the placement of J.
    At this point, either G or L can be third.
  If M is somewhere before J and somewhere before K, the only possibility is K in position 7, and L in position 3.
  Therefore, the answer is B: L third.

  B: Undergraduates who go to Nanyang University to study for a master's degree without a test may not obtain the recommended qualifications of their schools.

Choices:
  A: Obese people are more likely to suffer from heart disease than people with normal weight.However, obese people make up a very small percentage of our population.Therefore, in our country, there is no need for the medical and health community to emphasize the risk of heart disease.
  B: Unchecked sex is more likely to be infected with AIDS than checkpoint.However, among people with unchecked sex, only a small percentage of people are infected with AIDS.Therefore, there is no need to emphasize the harm of unchecked sex in the propaganda of AIDS prevention.
  C: The prevailing view is that smoking is more likely to cause lung cancer than not smoking.However, in some countries, the proportion of people with lung cancer who have a history of smoking is not higher than the proportion of the total population who have a history of smoking.Therefore, the above popular opinion is likely to be a prejudice.

Topic: Logic
Context: A company has a 6-story office building.The company's finance department, planning department, administration department, sales department, human resources department, and research and development department work here, and each department occupies one of the floors.Known? (1) The two floors of the human resources department and the sales department are not adjacent; (2) The finance department is on the next floor of the planning department; (3) The floor of the administrative department is above the planning department, but in the manpower Below the Resources Department.
Question: If the Finance Department is on the third level, which of the following may be correct?
Choices:
  A: The R & D department is on the fifth floor
  B: The R & D department is on the upper level of the sales department
  C: The Administration Department is not on the upper level of the Planning Department
  D: The sales department is on a certain layer above the planning department
Response 0:
Thought:
  The finance department is on the next floor of the planning department. Finance department is on the 3rd floor. Therefore, the planning department can be either on the 2nd or 4th floor.
  The floor of the administrative department is above the planning department. Hence, the administration department is on the 4th or 5th floor if planning department is on the 2nd floor or on the 3rd or 5th floor if planning department is on the 4th floor.
  The two floors of the human resources department and the sales department are not adjacent. So, one of the departments is on the 1st or 2nd floor while the other is on the 4th or 5th floor.
  
  A: The R & D department is on the fifth floor. Incorrect as there are only six floors in the building. 
  B: The R & D department is on the upper level of the sales department. Cannot be determined with certainty.
  C: The Administration Department is not on the upper level of the Planning Department. Incorrect as per the given information as the floor of the administration department is above the planning department.
  D: The sales department is on a certain layer above the planning department. Correct. If planning department is on the 2nd floor, sales department can be on the 4th floor. If planning department is on the 4th floor, sales department can be on the 6th floor.
 
Therefore, the answer is D: The sales department is on a certain layer above the planning department. 

Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  According to the premise, six floors are assigned to six different departments.
  The finance department is on the next floor of the planning department, which means the finance department and the planning department should occupy adjacent floors.
  According to the premise that the R&D department and the sales department floors are not adjacent, the R&D department and sales department floors should either have one or more floors between them, or be on the top and bottom of each other.
  If the finance department is on the third level, the planning department should be on the second floor. 
  According to the premise, the administrative department is above the planning department and below the human resources department. 
  Therefore, the administration department can only be on the fourth and fifth floors.
  The R&D department is left with the first and sixth floors, and since the sales department and the R&D department floors are not adjacent, it can only be inferred that the R&D department is on the first floor.
  Therefore, choice A is incorrect. 
  As mentioned above, the R&D department and sales department floors should either have one or more floors between them, or be on the top and bottom of each other. Therefore, choice B is incorrect.
  We can infer that the administration department is on the fifth floor, which means the option C is incorrect.
  If the sales department is on the fifth floor, then the planning department can only be on the fourth floor, which violates the premises as the finance department is on the next floor of the planning department. Therefore, the option D is incorrect.
  None of the given options are correct.

  The sales department and human resources department are not adjacent so the sales department cannot be on the 2nd or the 4th floor. Therefore, it can only be on the 1st, 5th or 6th floor.
  Since the research and development department cannot be adjacent to the sales department, it can only be on the 2nd or 4th floor.
  Therefore, the only possible option is C: The Administration Department is not on the upper level of the Planning Department.

Response 9:
Thought:
  The finance department is on the third level.
  The planning department is on either the second or the fourth floor.
  The human resources department and the sales department are not adjacent.
  The administrative department is above the planning department.
  The Research and Development (R&D) department is on one of the floors.
  Options:
    A: The R&D department is on the fifth floor.
      There are only six floors in the building. If the R&D department is on the fifth floor, then only one floor remains for the sales department and human resources department. However, the human resources department and the sales department are not adjacent, which means there is no floor available for the sales department to occupy. Therefore, the R&D department cannot be on the fifth floor.
    B: The R&D Department is on the upper level of the sales department.
      The sales department and the human resources department can occupy either the fourth and fifth floors or the fifth and sixth floors. If the R&D department is on the top floor, it can be on the sixth floor, and the sales department can be on the fifth floor. Therefore, this option is possible.
    C: The Administration Department is not on the upper level of the Planning Department.
      Since the finance department is on the third level and the administrative department is above the planning department and below the human resources department, the administrative department needs to be on the fifth or sixth floor. Therefore, this option is not possible.
    D: The sales department is on a certain layer above the planning department.
      If the sales department is one floor above the planning department, it would be on the fourth floor. Then the human resources department needs to occupy the sixth floor. However, if the human resources department is on the sixth floor, the R&D department can only be on the fifth floor, which violates statement A. Therefore, this option is not correct.
    Therefore, the only correct answer is B.
